<p><b>PHP</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Server-side_scripting" title="Server-side scripting">server-side scripting</a> language designed primarily for <a href="/wiki/Web_development" title="Web development">web development</a> but also used as a <a href="/wiki/General-purpose_programming_language" title="General-purpose programming language">general-purpose programming language</a>. Originally created by <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a> in 1994,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_of_PHP_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_PHP-5">[5]</a></sup> the PHP <a href="/wiki/Reference_implementation" title="Reference implementation">reference implementation</a> is now produced by The PHP Development Team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup> PHP originally stood for <i>Personal Home Page</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-History_of_PHP_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-History_of_PHP-5">[5]</a></sup> but it now stands for the <a href="/wiki/Recursive_acronym" title="Recursive acronym">recursive acronym</a> <i>PHP: Hypertext Preprocessor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP code may be embedded into <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> code, or it can be used in combination with various <a href="/wiki/Web_template_system" title="Web template system">web template systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_content_management_system" title="Web content management system">web content management systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Web_framework" title="Web framework">web frameworks</a>. PHP code is usually processed by a PHP <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreter</a> implemented as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plugin_(computing)" title="Plugin (computing)">module</a> in the web server or as a <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">Common Gateway Interface</a> (CGI) executable. The web server combines the results of the interpreted and executed PHP code, which may be any type of data, including images, with the generated web page. PHP code may also be executed with a <a href="/wiki/Command-line_interface" title="Command-line interface">command-line interface</a> (CLI) and can be used to implement <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_software" title="Computer software">standalone</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical applications</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The standard PHP interpreter, powered by the <a href="/wiki/Zend_Engine" title="Zend Engine">Zend Engine</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a> released under the <a href="/wiki/PHP_License" title="PHP License">PHP License</a>. PHP has been widely ported and can be deployed on most web servers on almost every <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">platform</a>, free of charge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foundations_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-foundations-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The PHP language evolved without a written <a href="/wiki/Formal_specification" title="Formal specification">formal specification</a> or standard until 2014, leaving the canonical PHP interpreter as a <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> standard. Since 2014 work has gone on to create a formal PHP specification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;max-width:327px">
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:107px;max-width:107px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="669" data-file-width="495" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg/105px-Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg/158px-Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg/210px-Rasmus_Lerdorf_cropped.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:107px;max-width:107px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="597" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg/105px-Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg/158px-Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg/210px-Andi_Gutmans_1.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:107px;max-width:107px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="298" data-file-width="220" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg/105px-Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg/158px-Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg/210px-Zeev_Suraski_2005_cropped.jpg 2x" width="105"/></a></div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a> (left), who wrote the original <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">Common Gateway Interface</a> (CGI) component, together with <a href="/wiki/Andi_Gutmans" title="Andi Gutmans">Andi Gutmans</a> (middle) and <a href="/wiki/Zeev_Suraski" title="Zeev Suraski">Zeev Suraski</a> (right), who rewrote the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parser" title="Parser">parser</a> that formed PHP 3.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>PHP development began in 1995 when <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a> wrote several <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">Common Gateway Interface</a> (CGI) programs in C,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php_origins_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-php_origins-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> which he used to maintain his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Personal_homepage" title="Personal homepage">personal homepage</a>. He extended them to work with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_form" title="Web form">web forms</a> and to communicate with <a href="/wiki/Database" title="Database">databases</a>, and called this implementation "Personal Home Page/Forms Interpreter" or PHP/FI.</p>
<p>PHP/FI could help to build simple, dynamic <a href="/wiki/Web_application" title="Web application">web applications</a>. To accelerate <a href="/wiki/Software_bug" title="Software bug">bug</a> reporting and to improve the code, Lerdorf initially announced the release of PHP/FI as "Personal Home Page Tools (PHP Tools) version 1.0" on the <a href="/wiki/Usenet" title="Usenet">Usenet</a> discussion group <i>comp.infosystems.www.authoring.cgi</i> on June 8, 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> This release already had the basic functionality that PHP has as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. This included <a href="/wiki/Local_variable#Local_variables_in_Perl" title="Local variable">Perl-like variables</a>, form handling, and the ability to embed HTML. The <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">syntax</a> resembled that of Perl but was simpler, more limited and less consistent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lerdorf did not intend the early PHP to become a new programming language, but it grew organically, with Lerdorf noting in retrospect: "I don’t know how to stop it, there was never any intent to write a programming language […] I have absolutely no idea how to write a programming language, I just kept adding the next logical step on the way."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-itconversations_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-itconversations-16">[16]</a></sup> A development team began to form and, after months of work and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_development_stage" title="Beta development stage">beta</a> testing, officially released PHP/FI 2 in November 1997.</p>
<p><span id="ORGANIC"></span> The fact that PHP lacked an original overall design but instead developed organically has led to inconsistent naming of functions and inconsistent ordering of their parameters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> In some cases, the function names were chosen to match the lower-level libraries which PHP was "wrapping",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> while in some very early versions of PHP the length of the function names was used internally as a <a href="/wiki/Hash_function" title="Hash function">hash function</a>, so names were chosen to improve the distribution of hash values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php-internals-70691_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-php-internals-70691-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PHP_3_and_4">PHP 3 and 4</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: PHP 3 and 4">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zeev_Suraski" title="Zeev Suraski">Zeev Suraski</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andi_Gutmans" title="Andi Gutmans">Andi Gutmans</a> rewrote the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parser" title="Parser">parser</a> in 1997 and formed the base of PHP 3, changing the language's name to the <a href="/wiki/Recursive_acronym" title="Recursive acronym">recursive acronym</a> <i>PHP: Hypertext Preprocessor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Afterwards, public testing of PHP 3 began, and the official launch came in June 1998. Suraski and Gutmans then started a new <a href="/wiki/Rewrite_(programming)" title="Rewrite (programming)">rewrite</a> of PHP's core, producing the <a href="/wiki/Zend_Engine" title="Zend Engine">Zend Engine</a> in 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> They also founded <a href="/wiki/Zend_Technologies" title="Zend Technologies">Zend Technologies</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ramat_Gan" title="Ramat Gan">Ramat Gan</a>, Israel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 22, 2000, PHP 4, powered by the Zend Engine 1.0, was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup> As of August 2008 this branch reached version 4.4.9. PHP 4 is no longer under development nor will any security updates be released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007_news_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007_news-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PHP_5">PHP 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: PHP 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On July 13, 2004, PHP 5 was released, powered by the new Zend Engine II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup> PHP 5 included new features such as improved support for <a href="/wiki/Object-oriented_programming" title="Object-oriented programming">object-oriented programming</a>, the PHP Data Objects (PDO) extension (which defines a lightweight and consistent interface for accessing databases), and numerous performance enhancements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> In 2008 PHP 5 became the only stable version under development. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Late_static_binding" title="Late static binding">Late static binding</a> had been missing from PHP and was added in version 5.3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many high-profile open-source projects ceased to support PHP 4 in new code as of February 5, 2008, because of the GoPHP5 initiative,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gophp5_projects_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-gophp5_projects-27">[27]</a></sup> provided by a consortium of PHP developers promoting the transition from PHP 4 to PHP 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gophp5_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-gophp5-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over time, PHP interpreters became available on most existing <a href="/wiki/32-bit" title="32-bit">32-bit</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/64-bit" title="64-bit">64-bit</a> operating systems, either by building them from the PHP source code, or by using pre-built binaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> For the PHP versions 5.3 and 5.4, the only available <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> binary distributions were 32-bit <a href="/wiki/X86" title="X86">x86</a> builds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> requiring Windows 32-bit compatibility mode while using <a href="/wiki/Internet_Information_Services" title="Internet Information Services">Internet Information Services</a> (IIS) on a 64-bit Windows platform. PHP version 5.5 made the 64-bit <a href="/wiki/X86-64" title="X86-64">x86-64</a> builds available for Microsoft Windows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PHP_6_and_Unicode"><span id="PHP6-UNICODE"></span>PHP 6 and Unicode</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: PHP 6 and Unicode">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>PHP has received criticism due to lacking native <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> support at the core language level, instead only supporting byte strings. In 2005, a project headed by Andrei Zmievski was initiated to bring native Unicode support throughout PHP, by embedding the <a href="/wiki/International_Components_for_Unicode" title="International Components for Unicode">International Components for Unicode</a> (ICU) library, and representing text strings as <a href="/wiki/UTF-16" title="UTF-16">UTF-16</a> internally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Since this would cause major changes both to the internals of the language and to user code, it was planned to release this as version 6.0 of the language, along with other major features then in development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, a shortage of developers who understood the necessary changes, and performance problems arising from conversion to and from UTF-16, which is rarely used in a web context, led to delays in the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> As a result, a PHP 5.3 release was created in 2009, with many non-Unicode features back-ported from PHP 6, notably namespaces. In March 2010, the project in its current form was officially abandoned, and a PHP 5.4 release was prepared containing most remaining non-Unicode features from PHP 6, such as traits and closure re-binding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Initial hopes were that a new plan would be formed for Unicode integration, but as of 2014 none have been adopted.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PHP_7"><span id="NG"></span><span id="ZE3"></span><span id="PHP7"></span>PHP 7</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: PHP 7">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During 2014 and 2015, a new major PHP version was developed, which was numbered PHP 7. The numbering of this version involved some debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> While the PHP 6 Unicode experiment had never been released, several articles and book titles referenced the PHP 6 name, which might have caused confusion if a new release were to reuse the name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> After a vote, the name PHP 7 was chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>The foundation of PHP 7 is a PHP <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Branching_(revision_control)" title="Branching (revision control)">branch</a> that was originally dubbed <i>PHP next generation</i> (<i>phpng</i>). It was authored by Dmitry Stogov, Xinchen Hui and Nikita Popov,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and aimed to optimize PHP performance by refactoring the Zend Engine to use more compact <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Data_structures" title="Data structures">data structures</a> with improved <a href="/wiki/Locality_of_reference" title="Locality of reference">cache locality</a> while retaining near-complete language compatibility.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> As of 14 July 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a>-based benchmarks, which served as the main benchmark suite for the phpng project, showed an almost 100% increase in performance. Changes from phpng are also expected to make it easier to improve performance in the future, as more compact data structures and other changes are seen as better suited for a successful migration to a <a href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compilation" title="Just-in-time compilation">just-in-time</a> (JIT) compiler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phpng_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-phpng-43">[43]</a></sup> Because of the significant changes, the reworked Zend Engine is called <i>Zend Engine 3</i>, succeeding Zend Engine 2 used in PHP 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZE2_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZE2-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of major internal changes in phpng, it must receive a new <a href="/wiki/Software_versioning" title="Software versioning">major version</a> number of PHP, rather than a minor PHP 5 release, according to PHP's release process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-releaseprocess_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-releaseprocess-45">[45]</a></sup> Major versions of PHP are allowed to break backward-compatibility of code and therefore PHP 7 presented an opportunity for other improvements beyond phpng that require backward-compatibility breaks, including wider use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exception_(computer_science)" title="Exception (computer science)">exceptions</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-engine_exceptions_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-engine_exceptions-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> reworking variable syntax to be more consistent and complete,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uvs_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-uvs-48">[48]</a></sup> and the deprecation or removal of various legacy features.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP 7 also introduced new language features, including return type declarations for functions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-return-types_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-return-types-51">[51]</a></sup> which complement the existing parameter type declarations, and support for the scalar types (integer, float, string, and boolean) in parameter and return type declarations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scalar-types_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-scalar-types-52">[52]</a></sup></p>

<td style="background:salmon;">4.2</td>

<td>Disabled <code>register_globals</code> by default. Data received over the network is not inserted directly into the <a href="/wiki/Global_variable" title="Global variable">global</a> namespace anymore, closing possible security holes in applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php4changelog_54-2"><a href="#cite_note-php4changelog-54">[54]</a></sup></td>
