<tr>
<td style="background:#a0e75a;">7.1</td>
<td>1 December 2016<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php71schedule_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-php71schedule-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></td>
<td>1 December 2019<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supportedversions_61-2"><a href="#cite_note-supportedversions-61">[61]</a></sup></td>
<td><a href="/wiki/Void_type" title="Void type">void return type</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> class constant <a href="/wiki/Information_hiding" title="Information hiding">visibility modifiers</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nullable_type" title="Nullable type">nullable types</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Beginning on June 28, 2011, the PHP Group implemented a timeline for the release of new versions of PHP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-releaseprocess_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-releaseprocess-45">[45]</a></sup> Under this system, at least one release should occur every month. Once per year, a minor release should occur which may include new features. Every minor release should at least be supported for two years with security and bug fixes, followed by at least one year of only security fixes, for a total of a three-year release process for every minor release. No new features, unless small and self-contained, are to be introduced into a minor release during the three-year release process.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot"><span id="ELEPHPANT"></span>Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="240" data-file-width="350" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg/200px-Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg/300px-Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg/400px-Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Webysther_20160423_-_Elephpant.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The elePHPant, PHP mascot.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The mascot of the PHP project is the <i>elePHPant</i>, a blue <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephant</a> with the PHP logo on its side, designed by Vincent Pontier<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The elePHPant is sometimes differently colored when in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plush_toy" title="Plush toy">plush toy</a> form.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">Syntax</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Syntax">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/PHP_syntax_and_semantics" title="PHP syntax and semantics">PHP syntax and semantics</a></div>
<p>The following <a href="/wiki/%22Hello,_World!%22_program" title='"Hello, World!" program'>"Hello, World!" program</a> is written in PHP code embedded in an <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> document:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="x">&lt;!DOCTYPE html&gt;</span>
<span class="x">&lt;html&gt;</span>
<span class="x">    &lt;head&gt;</span>
<span class="x">        &lt;title&gt;PHP Test&lt;/title&gt;</span>
<span class="x">    &lt;/head&gt;</span>
<span class="x">    &lt;body&gt;</span>
<span class="hll"><span class="x">        </span><span class="cp">&lt;?php</span> <span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s1">'&lt;p&gt;Hello World&lt;/p&gt;'</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="cp">?&gt;</span>
</span><span class="x">    &lt;/body&gt;</span>
<span class="x">&lt;/html&gt;</span>
</pre></div>
<p>However, as no requirement exists for PHP code to be embedded in HTML, the simplest version of <i>Hello, World!</i> may be written like this, with the closing tag omitted as preferred in files containing pure PHP code<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
 <span class="o">&lt;?=</span><span class="s1">'Hello world'</span><span class="p">;</span>
</pre></div>
<p>The PHP interpreter only executes PHP code within its <a href="/wiki/Delimiter" title="Delimiter">delimiters</a>. Anything outside its delimiters is not processed by PHP, although non-PHP text is still subject to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_structure" title="Control structure">control structures</a> described in PHP code. The most common delimiters are <i>&lt;?php</i> to open and <i>?&gt;</i> to close PHP sections. The shortened form <i>&lt;?</i> also exists. This short delimiter makes script files less portable, since support for them can be disabled in the local PHP configuration and it is therefore discouraged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfc-shortags_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-rfc-shortags-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-basic_syntax_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-basic_syntax-85">[85]</a></sup> However, there is no recommendation against the use of the echo short tag <i>&lt;?=</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Prior to PHP 5.4.0, this short syntax for <i>echo()</i> only works with the <i>short_open_tag</i> configuration setting enabled, while for PHP 5.4.0 and later it is always available.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfc-shortags_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-rfc-shortags-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> The purpose of all these delimiters is to separate PHP code from non-PHP content, such as <a href="/wiki/JavaScript" title="JavaScript">JavaScript</a> code or HTML markup.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first form of delimiters, <i>&lt;?php</i> and <i>?&gt;</i>, in <a href="/wiki/XHTML" title="XHTML">XHTML</a> and other <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> documents, creates correctly formed XML processing instructions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> This means that the resulting mixture of PHP code and other markup in the server-side file is itself well-formed XML.</p>
<p><span id="TYPE-HINTING"></span> Variables are prefixed with a <a href="/wiki/Dollar_sign" title="Dollar sign">dollar symbol</a>, and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primitive_type" title="Primitive type">type</a> does not need to be specified in advance. PHP 5 introduced <i>type hinting</i> that allows functions to force their parameters to be objects of a specific class, arrays, interfaces or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Callback_function" title="Callback function">callback functions</a>. However, before PHP 7.0, type hints could not be used with scalar types such as integer or string.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scalar-types_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-scalar-types-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike function and class names, variable names are case sensitive. Both double-quoted ("") and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heredoc" title="Heredoc">heredoc</a> strings provide the ability to interpolate a variable's value into the string.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> PHP treats <a href="/wiki/Newline" title="Newline">newlines</a> as <a href="/wiki/Whitespace_character" title="Whitespace character">whitespace</a> in the manner of a <a href="/wiki/Free-form_language" title="Free-form language">free-form language</a>, and statements are terminated by a semicolon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> PHP has three types of <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_programming_languages_(syntax)#Comments" title="Comparison of programming languages (syntax)">comment syntax</a>: <code>/* */</code> marks block and inline comments; <code>//</code> as well as <code>#</code> are used for one-line comments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The <code>echo</code> statement is one of several facilities PHP provides to output text, <i>e.g.</i>, to a web browser.</p>
<p>In terms of keywords and language syntax, PHP is similar to the C style syntax. <i>if</i> conditions, <i>for</i> and <i>while</i> loops, and function returns are similar in syntax to languages such as C, C++, C#, Java and Perl.</p>
<p>The following is an example of PHP for loop:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="cp">&lt;?php</span> 
<span class="k">for</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$x</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="mi">0</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nv">$x</span> <span class="o">&lt;=</span> <span class="mi">100</span><span class="p">;</span> <span class="nv">$x</span><span class="o">++</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>
    <span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s2">"The number is: </span><span class="si">$x</span><span class="s2"> &lt;br&gt;"</span><span class="p">;</span>
<span class="p">}</span> 
<span class="cp">?&gt;</span>
</pre></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_types">Data types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Data types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>PHP stores integers in a platform-dependent range, either a 64-bit or 32-bit <a href="/wiki/Signed_number_representations" title="Signed number representations">signed</a> <a href="/wiki/Integer_(computer_science)" title="Integer (computer science)">integer</a> equivalent to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C_variable_types_and_declarations" title="C variable types and declarations">C-language long type</a>. Unsigned integers are converted to signed values in certain situations; this behavior is different from that of other programming languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Integer variables can be assigned using decimal (positive and negative), <a href="/wiki/Octal" title="Octal">octal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hexadecimal" title="Hexadecimal">hexadecimal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Binary_code" title="Binary code">binary</a> notations.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Floating_point" title="Floating point">Floating point</a> numbers are also stored in a platform-specific range. They can be specified using floating point notation, or two forms of <a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">scientific notation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-types-95">[95]</a></sup> PHP has a native <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boolean_datatype" title="Boolean datatype">Boolean</a> type that is similar to the native Boolean types in <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>. Using the Boolean type conversion rules, non-zero values are interpreted as true and zero as false, as in <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a> and C++.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-types-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>The null data type represents a variable that has no value; <code>NULL</code> is the only allowed value for this data type.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-types-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Variables of the "resource" type represent references to resources from external sources. These are typically created by functions from a particular extension, and can only be processed by functions from the same extension; examples include file, image, and database resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_95-3"><a href="#cite_note-types-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>Arrays can contain elements of any type that PHP can handle, including resources, objects, and other arrays. Order is preserved in lists of values and in <a href="/wiki/Hash_table" title="Hash table">hashes</a> with both keys and values, and the two can be intermingled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-types_95-4"><a href="#cite_note-types-95">[95]</a></sup> PHP also supports <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/String_(computing)" title="String (computing)">strings</a>, which can be used with single quotes, double quotes, nowdoc or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heredoc" title="Heredoc">heredoc</a> syntax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Standard PHP Library (SPL) attempts to solve standard problems and implements efficient data access interfaces and classes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Functions">Functions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Functions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>PHP defines a large array of functions in the core language and many are also available in various extensions; these functions are well documented in the online PHP documentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-functions_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-functions-98">[98]</a></sup> However, the built-in library has a wide variety of naming conventions and associated inconsistencies, as described under <a href="#ORGANIC">history</a> above.</p>
<p>Custom functions may be defined by the developer, e.g.:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">myAge</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$birthYear</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>                                  <span class="c1">// defines a function, this one is named "myAge"</span>
    <span class="nv">$yearsOld</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nb">date</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'Y'</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">-</span> <span class="nv">$birthYear</span><span class="p">;</span>                       <span class="c1">// calculates the age</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="nv">$yearsOld</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="s1">' year'</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$yearsOld</span> <span class="o">!=</span> <span class="mi">1</span> <span class="o">?</span> <span class="s1">'s'</span> <span class="o">:</span> <span class="s1">''</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="c1">// returns the age in a descriptive form</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s1">'I am currently '</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="nx">myAge</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">1981</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="s1">' old.'</span><span class="p">;</span>               <span class="c1">// outputs the text concatenated</span>
                                                              <span class="c1">// with the return value of myAge()</span>
<span class="c1">// As the result of this syntax, myAge() is called.</span>
</pre></div>
<p>In 2017, the output of the above sample program is 'I am currently 36 years old.'</p>
<p>In lieu of <a href="/wiki/Function_pointer" title="Function pointer">function pointers</a>, functions in PHP can be referenced by a string containing their name. In this manner, normal PHP functions can be used, for example, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Callback_function" title="Callback function">callbacks</a> or within <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Function_table" title="Function table">function tables</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variable-functions_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-variable-functions-99">[99]</a></sup> User-defined functions may be created at any time without being <a href="/wiki/Function_prototype" title="Function prototype">prototyped</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-functions_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-functions-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variable-functions_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-variable-functions-99">[99]</a></sup> Functions may be defined inside code blocks, permitting a <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_dispatch" title="Dynamic dispatch">run-time decision</a> as to whether or not a function should be defined. There is a <code>function_exists</code> function that determines whether a function with a given name has already been defined. Function calls must use parentheses, with the exception of zero-argument class <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constructor_(computer_science)" title="Constructor (computer science)">constructor</a> functions called with the PHP operator <i>new</i>, in which case parentheses are optional.</p>
<p>Until PHP 5.3, support for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anonymous_functions" title="Anonymous functions">anonymous functions</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Closure_(computer_science)" title="Closure (computer science)">closures</a> did not exist in PHP. While <code>create_function()</code> exists since PHP 4.0.1, it is merely a thin wrapper around <code>eval()</code> that allows normal PHP functions to be created during program execution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> PHP 5.3 added syntax to define an anonymous function or "closure"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> which can capture variables from the surrounding scope:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">getAdder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$x</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="k">function</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$y</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="k">use</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$x</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="nv">$x</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nv">$y</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="p">};</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="nv">$adder</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nx">getAdder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">8</span><span class="p">);</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$adder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="c1">// prints "10"</span>
</pre></div>
<p>In the example above, <code>getAdder()</code> function creates a closure using passed argument <code class="mw-highlight" dir="ltr" id="" style=""><span class="nv">$x</span></code> (the keyword <code>use</code> imports a variable from the lexical context), which takes an additional argument <code class="mw-highlight" dir="ltr" id="" style=""><span class="nv">$y</span></code>, and returns the created closure to the caller. Such a function is a first-class object, meaning that it can be stored in a variable, passed as a parameter to other functions, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>Unusually for a dynamically typed language, PHP supports type declarations on function parameters, which are enforced at runtime. This has been supported for classes and interfaces since PHP 5.0, for arrays since PHP 5.1, for "callables" since PHP 5.4, and scalar (integer, float, string and boolean) types since PHP 7.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scalar-types_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-scalar-types-52">[52]</a></sup> PHP 7.0 also has type declarations for function return types, expressed by placing the type name after the list of parameters, preceded by a colon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-return-types_51-2"><a href="#cite_note-return-types-51">[51]</a></sup> For example, the <code>getAdder</code> function from the earlier example could be annotated with types like so in PHP 7:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">getAdder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">int</span> <span class="nv">$x</span><span class="p">)</span><span class="o">:</span> <span class="nx">\Closure</span> <span class="p">{</span>
    <span class="k">return</span> <span class="k">function</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nx">int</span> <span class="nv">$y</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="k">use</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$x</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">:</span> <span class="nx">int</span> <span class="p">{</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="nv">$x</span> <span class="o">+</span> <span class="nv">$y</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="p">};</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="nv">$adder</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nx">getAdder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">8</span><span class="p">);</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$adder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="mi">2</span><span class="p">);</span>        <span class="c1">// prints "10"</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$adder</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="k">null</span><span class="p">);</span>     <span class="c1">// throws an exception because an incorrect type was passed</span>
<span class="nv">$adder</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nx">getAdder</span><span class="p">([]);</span> <span class="c1">// would also throw an exception</span>
</pre></div>
<p>By default, scalar type declarations follow weak typing principles. So, for example, if a parameter's type is <code>int</code>, PHP would allow not only integers, but also convertible numeric strings, floats or booleans to be passed to that function, and would convert them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scalar-types_52-4"><a href="#cite_note-scalar-types-52">[52]</a></sup> However, PHP 7 has a "strict typing" mode which, when used, disallows such conversions for function calls and returns within a file.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scalar-types_52-5"><a href="#cite_note-scalar-types-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Object-oriented_programming">Object-oriented programming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Object-oriented programming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Basic <a href="/wiki/Object-oriented_programming" title="Object-oriented programming">object-oriented programming</a> functionality was added in PHP 3 and improved in PHP 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about_PHP_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-about_PHP-6">[6]</a></sup> This allowed for PHP to gain further abstraction, making creative tasks easier for programmers using the language. Object handling was completely rewritten for PHP 5, expanding the feature set and enhancing performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php_5_objects_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-php_5_objects-103">[103]</a></sup> In previous versions of PHP, objects were handled like <a href="/wiki/Value_type" title="Value type">value types</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php_5_objects_103-1"><a href="#cite_note-php_5_objects-103">[103]</a></sup> The drawback of this method was that code had to make heavy use of PHP's "reference" variables if it wanted to modify an object it was passed rather than creating a copy of it. In the new approach, objects are referenced by <a href="/wiki/Handle_(computing)" title="Handle (computing)">handle</a>, and not by value.</p>
<p>PHP 5 introduced private and protected <a href="/wiki/Member_variable" title="Member variable">member variables</a> and methods, along with <a href="/wiki/Abstract_type" title="Abstract type">abstract classes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_type" title="Final type">final classes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abstract_method" title="Abstract method">abstract methods</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_method" title="Final method">final methods</a>. It also introduced a standard way of declaring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constructor_(computer_science)" title="Constructor (computer science)">constructors</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Destructor_(computer_science)" title="Destructor (computer science)">destructors</a>, similar to that of other object-oriented languages such as <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>, and a standard <a href="/wiki/Exception_handling" title="Exception handling">exception handling</a> model. Furthermore, PHP 5 added <a href="/wiki/Interface_(computing)" title="Interface (computing)">interfaces</a> and allowed for multiple interfaces to be implemented. There are special interfaces that allow objects to interact with the runtime system. <a href="/wiki/Object_(computer_science)" title="Object (computer science)">Objects</a> implementing ArrayAccess can be used with <a href="/wiki/Array_data_type" title="Array data type">array</a> syntax and objects implementing <a href="/wiki/Iterator" title="Iterator">Iterator</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IteratorAggregate" title="IteratorAggregate">IteratorAggregate</a> can be used with the <code>foreach</code> <a href="/wiki/Language_construct" title="Language construct">language construct</a>. There is no <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_table" title="Virtual table">virtual table</a> feature in the engine, so <a href="/wiki/Static_variable" title="Static variable">static variables</a> are bound with a name instead of a reference at compile time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zend_engine_2_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-zend_engine_2-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>If the developer creates a copy of an object using the reserved word <code>clone</code>, the Zend engine will check whether a <code>__clone()</code> method has been defined. If not, it will call a default <code>__clone()</code> which will copy the object's properties. If a <code>__clone()</code> method is defined, then it will be responsible for setting the necessary properties in the created object. For convenience, the engine will supply a function that imports the properties of the source object, so the programmer can start with a by-value <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/replica" title="wikt:replica">replica</a> of the source object and only override properties that need to be changed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>The following is a basic example of <a href="/wiki/Object-oriented_programming" title="Object-oriented programming">object-oriented programming</a> in PHP:</p>
<div class="mw-highlight mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr">
<pre>
<span class="k">class</span> <span class="nc">Person</span>
<span class="p">{</span>
    <span class="k">public</span> <span class="nv">$firstName</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="k">public</span> <span class="nv">$lastName</span><span class="p">;</span>

    <span class="k">public</span> <span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">__construct</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$firstName</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">$lastName</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="s1">''</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span> <span class="c1">// optional second argument</span>
        <span class="nv">$this</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">firstName</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nv">$firstName</span><span class="p">;</span>
        <span class="nv">$this</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">lastName</span>  <span class="o">=</span> <span class="nv">$lastName</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="p">}</span>

    <span class="k">public</span> <span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">greet</span><span class="p">()</span> <span class="p">{</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="s1">'Hello, my name is '</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="nv">$this</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">firstName</span> <span class="o">.</span>
               <span class="p">((</span><span class="nv">$this</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">lastName</span> <span class="o">!=</span> <span class="s1">''</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">?</span> <span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">' '</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="nv">$this</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">lastName</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">:</span> <span class="s1">''</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="s1">'.'</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="p">}</span>

    <span class="k">public</span> <span class="k">static</span> <span class="k">function</span> <span class="nf">staticGreet</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="nv">$firstName</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="nv">$lastName</span><span class="p">)</span> <span class="p">{</span>
        <span class="k">return</span> <span class="s1">'Hello, my name is '</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="nv">$firstName</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="s1">' '</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="nv">$lastName</span> <span class="o">.</span> <span class="s1">'.'</span><span class="p">;</span>
    <span class="p">}</span>
<span class="p">}</span>

<span class="nv">$he</span>    <span class="o">=</span> <span class="k">new</span> <span class="nx">Person</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'John'</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'Smith'</span><span class="p">);</span>
<span class="nv">$she</span>   <span class="o">=</span> <span class="k">new</span> <span class="nx">Person</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'Sally'</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'Davis'</span><span class="p">);</span>
<span class="nv">$other</span> <span class="o">=</span> <span class="k">new</span> <span class="nx">Person</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'iAmine'</span><span class="p">);</span>

<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$he</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">greet</span><span class="p">();</span> <span class="c1">// prints "Hello, my name is John Smith."</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s1">'&lt;br /&gt;'</span><span class="p">;</span>

<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$she</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">greet</span><span class="p">();</span> <span class="c1">// prints "Hello, my name is Sally Davis."</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s1">'&lt;br /&gt;'</span><span class="p">;</span>

<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nv">$other</span><span class="o">-&gt;</span><span class="na">greet</span><span class="p">();</span> <span class="c1">// prints "Hello, my name is iAmine."</span>
<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="s1">'&lt;br /&gt;'</span><span class="p">;</span>

<span class="k">echo</span> <span class="nx">Person</span><span class="o">::</span><span class="na">staticGreet</span><span class="p">(</span><span class="s1">'Jane'</span><span class="p">,</span> <span class="s1">'Doe'</span><span class="p">);</span> <span class="c1">// prints "Hello, my name is Jane Doe."</span>
</pre></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visibility_(computer_science)" title="Visibility (computer science)">visibility</a> of PHP properties and methods is defined using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keyword_(computer_programming)" title="Keyword (computer programming)">keywords</a> <code>public</code>, <code>private</code>, and <code>protected</code>. The default is public, if only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Variable_(programming)" title="Variable (programming)">var</a> is used; <code>var</code> is a synonym for <code>public</code>. Items declared <code>public</code> can be accessed everywhere. <code>protected</code> limits access to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inherited_class" title="Inherited class">inherited classes</a> (and to the class that defines the item). <code>private</code> limits visibility only to the class that defines the item.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Objects of the same type have access to each other's private and protected members even though they are not the same instance. PHP's member visibility features have sometimes been described as "highly useful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> However, they have also sometimes been described as "at best irrelevant and at worst positively harmful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Implementations">Implementations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Implementations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The original, only complete and most widely used PHP implementation is powered by the <a href="/wiki/Zend_Engine" title="Zend Engine">Zend Engine</a> and known simply as PHP. To disambiguate it from other implementations, it is sometimes unofficially referred to as "Zend PHP". The Zend Engine <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compiles</a> PHP <a href="/wiki/Source_code" title="Source code">source code</a> on-the-fly into an internal format that it can execute, thus it works as an <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> It is also the "reference implementation" of PHP, as PHP has no formal specification, and so the semantics of Zend PHP define the semantics of PHP itself. Due to the complex and nuanced semantics of PHP, defined by how Zend works, it is difficult for competing implementations to offer complete compatibility.</p>
<p>PHP's single-request-per-script-execution model, and the fact the Zend Engine is an interpreter, leads to inefficiency; as a result, various products have been developed to help improve PHP performance. In order to speed up execution time and not have to compile the PHP source code every time the web page is accessed, PHP scripts can also be deployed in the PHP engine's internal format by using an <a href="/wiki/Opcode" title="Opcode">opcode</a> cache, which works by <a href="/wiki/Cache_(computing)" title="Cache (computing)">caching</a> the compiled form of a PHP script (opcodes) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shared_memory_(interprocess_communication)" title="Shared memory (interprocess communication)">shared memory</a> to avoid the overhead of <a href="/wiki/Parsing" title="Parsing">parsing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Compiling" title="Compiling">compiling</a> the code every time the script runs. An opcode cache, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zend_Opcache" title="Zend Opcache">Zend Opcache</a>, is built into PHP since version 5.5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Another example of a widely used opcode cache is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alternative_PHP_Cache" title="Alternative PHP Cache">Alternative PHP Cache</a> (APC), which is available as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PHP_Extension_Community_Library" title="PHP Extension Community Library">PECL</a> extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>While Zend PHP is still the most popular implementation, several other implementations have been developed. Some of these are <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compilers</a> or support <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JIT_compilation" title="JIT compilation">JIT compilation</a>, and hence offer performance benefits over Zend PHP at the expense of lacking full PHP compatibility. Alternative implementations include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/HipHop_Virtual_Machine" title="HipHop Virtual Machine">HipHop Virtual Machine</a> (HHVM) –  developed at Facebook and available as open source, it converts PHP code into a high-level bytecode (commonly known as an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intermediate_language" title="Intermediate language">intermediate language</a>), which is then translated into x86-64 machine code dynamically at runtime by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Just-in-time_compiler" title="Just-in-time compiler">just-in-time</a> (JIT) compiler, resulting in up to 6× performance improvements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Parrot_virtual_machine" title="Parrot virtual machine">Parrot</a> –  a virtual machine designed to run dynamic languages efficiently; Pipp transforms the PHP source code into the <a href="/wiki/Parrot_intermediate_representation" title="Parrot intermediate representation">Parrot intermediate representation</a>, which is then translated into the Parrot's bytecode and executed by the virtual machine.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phalanger_(compiler)" title="Phalanger (compiler)">Phalanger</a> –  compiles PHP into <a href="/wiki/Common_Intermediate_Language" title="Common Intermediate Language">Common Intermediate Language</a> (CIL) bytecode</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HipHop_for_PHP" title="HipHop for PHP">HipHop</a> –  developed at Facebook and available as open source, it transforms the PHP scripts into <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a> code and then compiles the resulting code, reducing the server load up to 50%. In early 2013, Facebook deprecated it in favor of HHVM due to multiple reasons, including deployment difficulties and lack of support for the whole PHP language, including the <tt>create_function()</tt> and <tt>eval()</tt> constructs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Licensing">Licensing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Licensing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>PHP is <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">free software</a> released under the <a href="/wiki/PHP_License" title="PHP License">PHP License</a>, which stipulates that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Products derived from this software may not be called "PHP", nor may "PHP" appear in their name, without prior written permission from group@php.net. You may indicate that your software works in conjunction with PHP by saying "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foo" title="Foo">Foo</a> for PHP" instead of calling it "PHP Foo" or "phpfoo".</p>
</blockquote>
<p>This restriction on use of "PHP" makes the PHP License incompatible with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Public_License" title="General Public License">General Public License</a> (GPL), while the Zend License is incompatible due to an advertising clause similar to that of the original <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BSD_license" title="BSD license">BSD license</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_and_community"><span id="PDO"></span><span id="ZEPHIR"></span>Development and community</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Development and community">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>PHP includes various <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_PHP_libraries" title="List of PHP libraries">free and open-source libraries</a> in its source distribution, or uses them in resulting PHP binary builds. PHP is fundamentally an <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>-aware system with built-in modules for accessing <a href="/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol" title="File Transfer Protocol">File Transfer Protocol</a> (FTP) servers and many database servers, including <a href="/wiki/PostgreSQL" title="PostgreSQL">PostgreSQL</a>, <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a> and <a href="/wiki/SQLite" title="SQLite">SQLite</a> (which is an embedded database), <a href="/wiki/Lightweight_Directory_Access_Protocol" title="Lightweight Directory Access Protocol">LDAP</a> servers, and others. Numerous functions familiar to C programmers, such as those in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stdio.h" title="Stdio.h">stdio</a> family, are available in standard PHP builds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP allows developers to write <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Software_extension" title="Software extension">extensions</a> in <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C</a> to add functionality to the PHP language. PHP extensions can be compiled statically into PHP or loaded dynamically at runtime. Numerous extensions have been written to add support for the <a href="/wiki/Windows_API" title="Windows API">Windows API</a>, process management on <a href="/wiki/Unix-like" title="Unix-like">Unix-like</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a>, multibyte strings (<a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a>), <a href="/wiki/CURL" title="CURL">cURL</a>, and several popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archive_format" title="Archive format">compression formats</a>. Other PHP features made available through extensions include integration with <a href="/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" title="Internet Relay Chat">IRC</a>, dynamic generation of images and <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Flash" title="Adobe Flash">Adobe Flash</a> content, <i>PHP Data Objects</i> (PDO) as an abstraction layer used for accessing databases,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> and even <a href="/wiki/Speech_synthesis" title="Speech synthesis">speech synthesis</a>. Some of the language's core functions, such as those dealing with strings and arrays, are also implemented as extensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PHP_Extension_Community_Library" title="PHP Extension Community Library">PHP Extension Community Library</a> (PECL) project is a repository for extensions to the PHP language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some other projects, such as <i>Zephir</i>, provide the ability for PHP extensions to be created in a high-level language and compiled into native PHP extensions. Such an approach, instead of writing PHP extensions directly in C, simplifies the development of extensions and reduces the time required for programming and testing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>The PHP Group consists of ten people (as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>): <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Thies_C._Arntzen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Thies C. Arntzen (page does not exist)">Thies C. Arntzen</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stig_Bakken&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stig Bakken (page does not exist)">Stig Bakken</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shane_Caraveo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shane Caraveo (page does not exist)">Shane Caraveo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andi_Gutmans" title="Andi Gutmans">Andi Gutmans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lerdorf" title="Rasmus Lerdorf">Rasmus Lerdorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sam_Ruby" title="Sam Ruby">Sam Ruby</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sascha_Schumann&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sascha Schumann (page does not exist)">Sascha Schumann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeev_Suraski" title="Zeev Suraski">Zeev Suraski</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jim_Winstead&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jim Winstead (page does not exist)">Jim Winstead</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andrei_Zmievski" title="Andrei Zmievski">Andrei Zmievski</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zend_Technologies" title="Zend Technologies">Zend Technologies</a> provides a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zend_Certified_Engineer" title="Zend Certified Engineer">PHP Certification</a> based on PHP 5.5<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> exam for programmers to become certified PHP developers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Installation_and_configuration"><span id="PHPFPM"></span>Installation and configuration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Installation and configuration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are two primary ways for adding support for PHP to a web server –  as a native web server module, or as a CGI executable. PHP has a direct module interface called <a href="/wiki/Server_Application_Programming_Interface" title="Server Application Programming Interface">Server Application Programming Interface</a> (SAPI), which is supported by many web servers including <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache HTTP Server</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microsoft_Internet_Information_Server" title="Microsoft Internet Information Server">Microsoft IIS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netscape" title="Netscape">Netscape</a> (now defunct) and <a href="/wiki/IPlanet" title="IPlanet">iPlanet</a>. Some other web servers, such as OmniHTTPd, support the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Server_Application_Programming_Interface" title="Internet Server Application Programming Interface">Internet Server Application Programming Interface</a> (ISAPI), which is a <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s web server module interface. If PHP has no module support for a web server, it can always be used as a <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">Common Gateway Interface</a> (CGI) or <a href="/wiki/FastCGI" title="FastCGI">FastCGI</a> processor; in that case, the web server is configured to use PHP's CGI executable to process all requests to PHP files.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-installation_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-installation-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP-FPM (FastCGI Process Manager) is an alternative FastCGI implementation for PHP, bundled with the official PHP distribution since version 5.3.3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> When compared to the older FastCGI implementation, it contains some additional features, mostly useful for heavily loaded web servers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>When using PHP for command-line scripting, a PHP <a href="/wiki/Command-line_interface" title="Command-line interface">command-line interface</a> (CLI) executable is needed. PHP supports a CLI SAPI as of PHP 4.3.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The main focus of this SAPI is developing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Command_line_interface" title="Command line interface">shell</a> applications using PHP. There are quite a few differences between the CLI SAPI and other SAPIs, although they do share many of the same behaviors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP has a direct module interface called SAPI for different web servers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php-installation2_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-php-installation2-135">[135]</a></sup> in case of PHP 5 and Apache 2.0 on Windows, it is provided in form of a <a href="/wiki/Dynamic-link_library" title="Dynamic-link library">DLL</a> file called <span style="font-family: monospace, monospace;">php5apache2.dll</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> which is a module that, among other functions, provides an interface between PHP and the web server, implemented in a form that the server understands. This form is what is known as a SAPI.</p>
<p>There are different kinds of SAPIs for various web server extensions. For example, in addition to those listed above, other SAPIs for the PHP language include the <a href="/wiki/Common_Gateway_Interface" title="Common Gateway Interface">Common Gateway Interface</a> (CGI) and <a href="/wiki/Command-line_interface" title="Command-line interface">command-line interface</a> (CLI).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-php-installation2_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-php-installation2-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP can also be used for writing desktop <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical user interface</a> (GUI) applications, by using the <a href="/wiki/PHP-GTK" title="PHP-GTK">PHP-GTK</a> extension. PHP-GTK is not included in the official PHP distribution,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-installation_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-installation-130">[130]</a></sup> and as an extension it can be used only with PHP versions 5.1.0 and newer. The most common way of installing PHP-GTK is compiling it from the source code.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>When PHP is installed and used in <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud</a> environments, <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">software development kits</a> (SDKs) are provided for using cloud-specific features. For example:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amazon_Web_Services" title="Amazon Web Services">Amazon Web Services</a> provides the AWS SDK for PHP<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Windows_Azure" title="Windows Azure">Windows Azure</a> can be used with the Windows Azure SDK for PHP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>Numerous configuration options are supported, affecting both core PHP features and extensions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> Configuration file <code>php.ini</code> is searched for in different locations, depending on the way PHP is used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> The configuration file is split into various sections,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> while some of the configuration options can be also set within the web server configuration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Use">Use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LAMP_software_bundle.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="1280" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/400px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/600px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/LAMP_software_bundle.svg/800px-LAMP_software_bundle.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LAMP_software_bundle.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A broad overview of the LAMP software bundle, displayed here together with <a href="/wiki/Squid_(software)" title="Squid (software)">Squid</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>PHP is a general-purpose scripting language that is especially suited to <a href="/wiki/Server-side_scripting" title="Server-side scripting">server-side</a> <a href="/wiki/Web_development" title="Web development">web development</a>, in which case PHP generally runs on a <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">web server</a>. Any PHP code in a requested file is <a href="/wiki/Execution_(computing)" title="Execution (computing)">executed</a> by the PHP runtime, usually to create <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_web_page" title="Dynamic web page">dynamic web page</a> content or dynamic images used on websites or elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> It can also be used for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Command-line" title="Command-line">command-line</a> scripting and <a href="/wiki/Client-side" title="Client-side">client-side</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical user interface</a> (GUI) applications. PHP can be deployed on most web servers, many <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Computing_platform" title="Computing platform">platforms</a>, and can be used with many <a href="/wiki/Relational_database_management_system" title="Relational database management system">relational database management systems</a> (RDBMS). Most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_hosting" title="Web hosting">web hosting</a> providers support PHP for use by their clients. It is available free of charge, and the PHP Group provides the complete source code for users to build, customize and extend for their own use.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foundations_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-foundations-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="1015" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg/400px-Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg/600px-Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg/800px-Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg.png 2x" width="400"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scheme_dynamic_page_en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dynamic web page: example of <a href="/wiki/Server-side_scripting" title="Server-side scripting">server-side scripting</a> (PHP and MySQL).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>PHP acts primarily as a <a href="/wiki/Filter_(software)" title="Filter (software)">filter</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> taking input from a file or stream containing text and/or PHP instructions and outputting another stream of data. Most commonly the output will be HTML, although it could be <a href="/wiki/JSON" title="JSON">JSON</a>, <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> or <a href="/wiki/Binary_data" title="Binary data">binary data</a> such as image or audio formats. Since PHP 4, the PHP <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parser" title="Parser">parser</a> <a href="/wiki/Compiler" title="Compiler">compiles</a> input to produce <a href="/wiki/Bytecode" title="Bytecode">bytecode</a> for processing by the <a href="/wiki/Zend_Engine" title="Zend Engine">Zend Engine</a>, giving improved performance over its <a href="/wiki/Interpreter_(computing)" title="Interpreter (computing)">interpreter</a> predecessor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Originally designed to create dynamic <a href="/wiki/Web_page" title="Web page">web pages</a>, PHP now focuses mainly on <a href="/wiki/Server-side_scripting" title="Server-side scripting">server-side scripting</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> and it is similar to other server-side scripting languages that provide dynamic content from a web server to a <a href="/wiki/Client_(computing)" title="Client (computing)">client</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>'s <a href="/wiki/ASP.NET" title="ASP.NET">ASP.NET</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>' <a href="/wiki/JavaServer_Pages" title="JavaServer Pages">JavaServer Pages</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> and <tt><a href="/wiki/Mod_perl" title="Mod perl">mod_perl</a></tt>. PHP has also attracted the development of many <a href="/wiki/Software_framework" title="Software framework">software frameworks</a> that provide building blocks and a design structure to promote <a href="/wiki/Rapid_application_development" title="Rapid application development">rapid application development</a> (RAD). Some of these include <a href="/wiki/PRADO_(framework)" title="PRADO (framework)">PRADO</a>, <a href="/wiki/CakePHP" title="CakePHP">CakePHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symfony" title="Symfony">Symfony</a>, <a href="/wiki/CodeIgniter" title="CodeIgniter">CodeIgniter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laravel" title="Laravel">Laravel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yii_Framework" title="Yii Framework">Yii Framework</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phalcon_(framework)" title="Phalcon (framework)">Phalcon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zend_Framework" title="Zend Framework">Zend Framework</a>, offering features similar to other <a href="/wiki/Web_framework" title="Web framework">web frameworks</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/LAMP_(software_bundle)" title="LAMP (software bundle)">LAMP architecture</a> has become popular in the web industry as a way of deploying web applications.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> PHP is commonly used as the <i>P</i> in this bundle alongside <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache</a> and <a href="/wiki/MySQL" title="MySQL">MySQL</a>, although the <i>P</i> may also refer to <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perl" title="Perl">Perl</a>, or some mix of the three. Similar packages, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WAMP_(software_bundle)" title="WAMP (software bundle)">WAMP</a> and <a href="/wiki/MAMP" title="MAMP">MAMP</a>, are also available for <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/MacOS" title="MacOS">macOS</a>, with the first letter standing for the respective operating system. Although both PHP and Apache are provided as part of the macOS base install, users of these packages seek a simpler installation mechanism that can be more easily kept up to date.</p>
<p>As of April 2007<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, over 20 million Internet domains had web services hosted on servers with PHP installed and <tt>mod_php</tt> was recorded as the most popular <a href="/wiki/Apache_HTTP_Server" title="Apache HTTP Server">Apache HTTP Server</a> module.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usage_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-usage-152">[152]</a></sup> As of October 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, PHP was used as the server-side programming language on 75% of all websites whose server-side programming language was known<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-W3Techs_usage_statistics_2010-10-29_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-W3Techs_usage_statistics_2010-10-29-153">[153]</a></sup> (as of February 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the percentage had reached 82%<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-W3Techs_usage_statistics_20140319_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-W3Techs_usage_statistics_20140319-154">[154]</a></sup>), and PHP was the most-used open source software within enterprises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Web_content_management_system" title="Web content management system">Web content management systems</a> written in PHP include <a href="/wiki/MediaWiki" title="MediaWiki">MediaWiki</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joomla" title="Joomla">Joomla</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/EZ_Publish" title="EZ Publish">eZ Publish</a>, <a href="/wiki/EZ_Platform" title="EZ Platform">eZ Platform</a>, <a href="/wiki/SilverStripe" title="SilverStripe">SilverStripe</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/WordPress" title="WordPress">WordPress</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Drupal" title="Drupal">Drupal</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Moodle" title="Moodle">Moodle</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> the user-facing portion of <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Digg" title="Digg">Digg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>For specific and more advanced usage scenarios, PHP offers a well defined and documented way for writing custom extensions in <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C</a> or <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B" title="C++">C++</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> Besides extending the language itself in form of additional <a href="/wiki/Library_(computing)" title="Library (computing)">libraries</a>, extensions are providing a way for improving execution speed where it is critical and there is room for improvements by using a true <a href="/wiki/Compiled_language" title="Compiled language">compiled language</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> PHP also offers well defined ways for embedding itself into other software projects. That way PHP can be easily used as an internal <a href="/wiki/Scripting_language" title="Scripting language">scripting language</a> for another project, also providing tight interfacing with the project's specific internal <a href="/wiki/Data_structure" title="Data structure">data structures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup></p>
<p>PHP received mixed reviews due to lacking support for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multithreading_(software)" title="Multithreading (software)">multithreading</a> at the core language level,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> though using threads is made possible by the "pthreads" <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PHP_Extension_Community_Library" title="PHP Extension Community Library">PECL</a> extension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of January 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, PHP was used in more than 240 million <a href="/wiki/Website" title="Website">websites</a> (39% of those sampled) and was installed on 2.1 million <a href="/wiki/Web_server" title="Web server">web servers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Security"><span id="REGISTER-GLOBALS"></span>Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=PHP&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2013, 9% of all vulnerabilities listed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Vulnerability_Database" title="National Vulnerability Database">National Vulnerability Database</a> were linked to PHP;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CVE_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-CVE-178">[178]</a></sup> historically, about 30% of all vulnerabilities listed since 1996 in this database are linked to PHP. Technical security flaws of the language itself or of its core libraries are not frequent; (these numbered 22 in 2009, which was about 1% of the total, although PHP applies to about 20% of programs listed.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PHP-related_vulnerabilities_on_the_National_Vulnerability_Database_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-PHP-related_vulnerabilities_on_the_National_Vulnerability_Database-179">[179]</a></sup> Recognizing that programmers make mistakes, some languages include <a href="/wiki/Taint_checking" title="Taint checking">taint checking</a> to automatically detect the lack of <a href="/wiki/Data_validation" title="Data validation">input validation</a> which induces many issues. Such a feature is being developed for PHP,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> but its inclusion into a release has been rejected several times in the past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are advanced protection patches, such as <a href="/wiki/Suhosin" title="Suhosin">Suhosin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hardening_(computing)" title="Hardening (computing)">Hardening</a>-Patch, that are especially designed for web hosting environments,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> primarily due to these environments being seen as places where carelessly written code may run.</p>
<p>There are certain language features and configuration parameters (primarily the default values for such runtime settings) that make PHP applications prone to security issues. Among these, <tt><a href="/wiki/Magic_quotes" title="Magic quotes">magic_quotes_gpc</a></tt> and <tt>register_globals</tt><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-register-globals_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-register-globals-184">[184]</a></sup> configuration directives are the best known; the latter made any URL parameters become PHP variables, opening a path for serious security vulnerabilities by allowing an attacker to set the value of any uninitialized global variable and interfere with the execution of a PHP script. Support for "<a href="/wiki/Magic_quotes" title="Magic quotes">magic quotes</a>" and "register globals" has been deprecated as of PHP 5.3.0, and removed as of PHP 5.4.0.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-magic-quotes_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-magic-quotes-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another example for the runtime settings vulnerability comes from failing to disable PHP execution (via <tt>engine</tt> configuration directive)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> for the directory where uploaded images are stored; leaving the default settings can result in execution of malicious PHP code embedded within the uploaded images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> Also, leaving enabled the dynamic loading of PHP extensions (via <tt>enable_dl</tt> configuration directive)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shared_web_hosting" title="Shared web hosting">shared web hosting</a> environment can lead to security issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also, implied <a href="/wiki/Type_conversion" title="Type conversion">type conversions</a> that result in incompatible values being treated as identical against the programmer's intent can lead to security issues. For example, the result of the comparison <i>0e1234 == 0</i> comparison is <i>true</i> because the first compared value is treated as <a href="/wiki/Scientific_notation" title="Scientific notation">scientific notation</a> having the value (<span class="nowrap">0<span style="margin-left:0.25em;margin-right:0.15em;">×</span>10<sup>1234</sup></span>), i.e. <i>zero</i>. This feature resulted in authentication vulnerabilities in <a href="/wiki/Simple_Machines_Forum" title="Simple Machines Forum">Simple Machines Forum</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Typo3" title="Typo3">Typo3</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/PhpBB" title="PhpBB">phpBB</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/MD5" title="MD5">MD5</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Password_hashing" title="Password hashing">password hashes</a> were compared. Instead, either the function <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strcmp" title="Strcmp">strcmp</a> or the identity operator (<i>===</i>) should be used; <i>0e1234 === 0</i> results in <i>false</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2013 analysis of over 170,000 <a href="/wiki/Website_defacement" title="Website defacement">website defacements</a>, published by <a href="/wiki/Zone-H" title="Zone-H">Zone-H</a>, the most frequently (53%) used technique was exploitation of <a href="/wiki/File_inclusion_vulnerability" title="File inclusion vulnerability">file inclusion vulnerability</a>, mostly related to insecure usage of the PHP functions <i>include</i>, <i>require</i>, and <i>allow_url_fopen</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup></p>
